ترجمہ اگر مدیون کا قرض دراہم ہوں اور مال بھی دراہم ہوں تو چکارے قاضی اس کی اجازت کے بغیر اور یہ بالاجماع ہے۔ کیونکہ قرض خواہ کو اسکی رضا کے بغیر لینے کا حق ہے تو قاضی اس کی مدد کر سکتا ہے۔ اور اگر قرض دراہم ہوں اور مال دنانیر یا اس کے برعکس ہو تو بیچ دے اس کو قاضی اس کے دین میں۔ اور یہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک استحسان ہے۔ قیاس یہ ہے کہ نہ بیچ سکے جیسے اسباب میں ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے دائن کو یہ اختیار نہیں کہ وہ اس کو جبر آلے لے۔ وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ وہ دونوں ثمنیت و مالیت میں متحد اور صورت میں مختلف ہیں ۔ پس اتحاد کے پیش نظر قاضی کیلئے ولایت تصرف ہے اور اختلاف کے لحاظ سے دائن سے لینے کی ولایت مسلوب ہے دونوں مشابہتوں پر عمل کرتے ہوئے بخلاف اسباب کے کہ ان کی ذات و صورت دونوں سے غرض متعلق ہوتی ہے۔ رہے نقود سو وہ صرف وسائل ہیں اور قرضہ میں پہلے نقود بیچے جائیں گے پھر اسباب پھر جائداد۔ پس جو سب سے زیادہ آسان ہو اس سے شروع کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس میں اداءِ قرض کی طرف مسارعت ہے جانب مدیون کی رعایت کے ساتھ اور اسکے بدنی کپڑوں میں سے ایک جوڑا چھوڑ کر باقی فروخت کر دیئے جائیں۔ کیونکہ اس میں کفایت ہے اور کہا گیا ہے کہ دو جوڑے۔ کیونکہ جب وہ اپنے کپڑے دھوئے گا تو پہننے کیلئے ضرور کچھ چاہئے۔ تشریح قوله و ان كان دينه ... الخ - اگر مدیون کا مال اور اس کا دین، دراہم یا دنانیر ہوں تو قاضی بلا امر مدیون دراہم ودنانیر سے قرض ادا کر دے۔ اسلئے کہ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر قرض خواہ اپنے قرضدار کے اسی جنس کے مال پر قابو پائے جس جنس کا قرضہ ہے تو وہ اپنے قرضہ کے بقدر مدیون کی رضامندی کے بغیر بھی لے سکتا ہے تو اسکو لینے کا حق پہلے ہی سے حاصل ہے۔ پس قاضی صرف مددگار ہوگا۔ جیسے اگر غائب کا ایسا مال موجود ہو جو اس کے اہل و عیال کے نفقہ واجبہ کی جنس سے ہے تو قاضی اعانت کر کے اس مال سے نفقہ دلوا دیتا ہے۔ قوله و له دنانير .... الخ - اور اگر مدیون کا مال دراہم ہوں اور دین دنانیر یا اس کا عکس ہو تو ان کو فروخت کر کے قرض ادا کر دے اور اس کا مال اسباب و جائداد ہو تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس کو فروخت نہ کرے صاحبین اور ائمہ ثلاثہ کے نزدیک اس کو بھی فروخت کر سکتا ہے۔

قوله وهذا عنه ابي حنيفة...... الخ - صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ نقود بیچنے کا جواز امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک استحسان ہے۔ قیاس یہ چاہتا ہے کہ قاضی اس کو فروخت نہ کر سکے جیسے اسباب میں ہوتا ہے اسی لئے قرض خواہ کو یہ اختیار نہیں کہ وہ اس نقد کو جبر آلے لے (جیسا که ابن ابی لیلی کہتے ہیں) وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ دراہم و دنانیر دونوں ثمن اور مالیت ہونے میں متحد ہیں۔ اسی لئے باب زکوۃ میں ایک کو دوسرے کے ساتھ منضم کر لیا جاتا ہے اور صورت میں دونوں مختلف ہیں۔ پس ثمنیت و مالیت میں اتحاد کے لحاظ سے تو قاضی اور غریم دونوں کیلئے ولایت تصرف ثابت ہوتی ہے اور صور مختلف ہونے کے اعتبار سے دونوں کیلئے ثابت نہیں ہوتی ۔ دونوں مشابہتوں پر عمل کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ متحد ہونے کے پیش نظر قاضی کو ولایت تصرف حاصل ہے اور اختلاف صورت کے پیش نظر قرض خواہ کو بلا رضا مندی لینے کا اختیار نہیں ہے۔ اور اس کا عکس اس لئے نہیں کیا گیا کہ قاضی کی ولایت ولایت غریم کی بہ نسبت اقولیٰ ہے۔ اور جب صورۃ مختلف ہونے کی صورت میں قاضی کیلئے ولایت ثابت نہیں ہوتی تو غریم کیلئے بطریق اولیٰ ثابت نہ ہوگی۔ پس دونوں مشابہتوں کا ابطال لازم آئے گا۔ فلهذا امتنع العكس -

صاحب ہدایہ نے و هذا عند ابی حنیفہ کہ کر ذکر امام ابوحنیفہ کی تصریح کی ہے۔ حالانکہ حکم بلا خلاف [؟] جماعی ہے۔ اس کی بابت بہت سے شراح ہدایہ نے یہ کہا ہے کہ چونکہ امام ابو حنیفہ قاضی کو مدیون کا اسباب فروخت کرنے کی اجازت نہیں دیتے تو شبہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے قول پر ہوتا ہے کہ نقدین میں بھی اجازت نہیں ہونی چاہئے۔ کیونکہ یہ بھی ایک نوع کی بیع ہے یعنی بیع صرف ہے۔ صاحب نتائج کہتے ہیں کہ توجیہ مذکور اس وقت نام ہو سکتی ہے جب وہذا عند ابی حنیفہ کے بعد لفظ استحسانا مذکور نہ ہوتا اور جب یہ لفظ مصرح موجود ہے تو حکم مذکور در حقیقت امام ابو حنیفہ ہی کے یہاں مخصوص ہوا۔ اسلئے بیع نقدین کا بطریق استحسانا جائز ہونا اور بطریق قیاس جائز نہ ہونا صرف امام ابو حنیفہ کا قول ہے صاحبین کے نزدیک بیع نقدین بطریق قیاس جائز ہے۔ فلا احتیاج الی الاعتذار قوله بخلاف العروض .... الخ امام ابوحنیفہ کے یہاں مدیون کا اسباب فروخت کرنے کی اجازت نہیں ہے۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک قاضی اس کا اسباب بھی فروخت کر سکتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ بیع نقود و بیع عروض کے درمیان وجہ فرق بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ اسباب کی صورت اور ذات دونوں سے غرض وابستہ ہوتی ہے۔ رہے نقود یعنی دراہم ودنانیر سو وہ تو صرف اسباب حاصل کرنے کا وسیلہ ہیں۔ پس نقود و اسباب میں فرق واضح ہے۔

قوله و يباع فى الدين ... الخ یہ تفریع صاحبین کے قول پر ہے۔ یعنی جب صاحبین کے نزدیک مدیون کا مال فروخت کرنا جائز ہوا تو مدیون کے قرضہ میں پہلے نقود فروخت کیئے جائیں گے۔ جبکہ قرضہ دراہم اور مدیون کا مال بھی نقد دراہم ہوں۔ پھر اسباب فروخت کیا جائے گا۔ پھر جائداد غرض جو سب سے آسان ہو اس سے ابتداء کی جائے گی۔ پھر اسی طرح درجہ بدرجہ فروخت کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس میں اداء قرض کی طرف مسارعت بھی ہے اور جانب مدیون کی رعایت بھی۔ اور مدیون کے پوشیدنی کپڑوں میں سے ایک جوڑا چھوڑ کر باقی کو فروخت کر دیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ پوشاک کیلئے ایک جوڑا کافی ہے اور بقول بعض مشائخ دو جوڑے چھوڑے جائیں گے۔ کیونکہ جب وہ کپڑے دھوئے گا تو ملبس کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔
Book of Interdiction. Translation: If the debtor's debt is dirhams and his property is also dirhams, then the qadi [pays] without his permission, and this is by consensus. Because the creditor has the right to take without his consent, so the qadi can help. And if the debt is dirhams and the property is dinars, or the opposite, then the qadi sells it for his debt. And this, according to Abu Hanifa, is istihsan. Qiyas would be that he cannot sell, like with goods. Therefore, the creditor does not have the option to take it forcibly. The reason for istihsan is that both are united in being price (thaman) and monetary value, but different in form. So, due to unity, the qadi has authority to dispose; due to difference, the creditor's authority to take is negated, acting on both similarities, unlike goods, where interest is attached to both essence and form. As for cash, it is only a means. And in debt, first cash is sold, then goods, then property. So, one starts with what is easiest, because there is haste towards debt payment along with consideration for the debtor. And from his body clothing, one set is left and the rest sold, because that suffices. And it is said: two sets, because when he washes his clothes, he needs something to wear. Commentary on 'and if his debt...': If the debtor's property and his debt are dirhams or dinars, the qadi pays the debt from dirhams and dinars without the debtor's command. Because the rule is that if the creditor gains control over the same type of property as his debt, he can take to the extent of his debt without the debtor's consent, so he already has the right to take. Thus the qadi is only an assistant. Similarly, if an absent person has property that is of the same type as the obligatory maintenance of his family, the qadi assists and provides maintenance from that property. Commentary on 'and he has dinars...': If the debtor's property is dirhams and the debt is dinars, or vice versa, they are sold and the debt is paid, and if his property is goods and real estate, then according to Abu Hanifa, he does not sell it; the Sahibayn and the three imams say he can sell it. Commentary on 'and this from Abu Hanifa...': The author of Hidayah says that the permissibility of selling cash is istihsan according to Abu Hanifa. Qiyas would require that the qadi cannot sell it, as with goods, and therefore the creditor does not have the option to take this cash forcibly (as Ibn Abi Layla says). The reason for istihsan is that dirhams and dinars are united in being price and monetary value; for this reason, in the chapter of zakat, one is combined with the other. But in form, they are different. So, due to unity in price and value, the qadi and the creditor both have authority to dispose; due to difference in form, both do not have it. Acting on both similarities, it is said that due to unity, the qadi has authority to dispose, and due to difference in form, the creditor does not have the option to take without consent. And the opposite is not done because the qadi's authority is stronger than the creditor's authority. And if the qadi's authority is not established in case of difference in form, then the creditor's is even less established. So nullification of both similarities would be necessary. Hence the opposite is prevented. The author of Hidayah saying 'this according to Abu Hanifa' specifies Abu Hanifa's view, although the ruling is [؟] consensus. Many commentators of Hidayah have said that since Abu Hanifa does not permit the qadi to sell goods, there is a doubt that he also does not permit selling cash, because it is also a type of sale, i.e., currency exchange. The author of Nata'ij says that the aforementioned justification can only be valid if after 'this according to Abu Hanifa' the word 'istihsanan' was not mentioned; but since this word is explicitly present, the ruling is specifically for Abu Hanifa. Therefore, the permissibility of selling cash by way of istihsan and its impermissibility by way of qiyas is only Abu Hanifa's statement; according to the Sahibayn, selling cash by qiyas is permissible. So there is no need for apology. Commentary on 'unlike goods...': According to Abu Hanifa, the qadi is not permitted to sell goods. According to the Sahibayn, the qadi can also sell goods. The author of Hidayah is explaining the reason for the difference between selling cash and selling goods: with goods, the purpose is attached to both their form and essence. As for cash, i.e., dirhams and dinars, they are only a means to acquire goods. So the difference between cash and goods is clear. Commentary on 'and he sells for debt...': This is a branch on the statement of the Sahibayn. That is, when according to the Sahibayn it is permissible to sell the debtor's property, then for his debt, first cash is sold (when the debt is dirhams and the property is also cash dirhams), then goods are sold, then property. In short, one starts with what is easiest. Then one sells in order, because this includes haste towards debt payment and consideration for the debtor. And from the debtor's clothing for covering, one set is left and the rest sold, because one set is sufficient for clothing. According to some scholars, two sets are left, because when he washes his clothes, it is necessary to have something to wear.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on Al-Hidayah discussing the rules for a qadi to sell a debtor's assets to pay debts. It begins by stating that if the debt and the debtor's property are of the same currency (e.g., both dirhams), the qadi can pay the debt without the debtor's permission by consensus (ijma). This is because the creditor has the right to take his due without the debtor's consent, so the qadi assists. If the debt is in one currency and the property in another (e.g., debt in dirhams, property in dinars), then according to Abu Hanifa, the qadi may sell the property by istihsan (juristic preference). The qiyas would disallow it, similar to goods. The reason for istihsan is that both are cash (thaman) and have monetary value in common, though their physical forms differ. Thus, due to their unity in being currency, the qadi has authority to sell; due to their difference in form, the creditor cannot take them forcibly. This is unlike goods, where both the essence and form matter. The commentary then discusses the order of sale: first cash, then goods, then property, starting with the most liquid. Regarding clothing, one set is left for the debtor; according to some scholars, two sets are left to allow for washing. The passage details the ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa does not allow selling goods; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and the three other imams (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) allow it. The commentator explains that Abu Hanifa's view is based on istihsan, while qiyas would prohibit selling cash as well. The Sahibayn permit selling cash by qiyas. The difference between cash and goods is that goods are desired for their specific essence and form, whereas cash is merely a means to acquire goods. Therefore, the order of sale is according to ease of conversion to the debt's currency.

Key Terms
حجر (hajr): Interdiction, legal restriction preventing a debtor from managing his property due to debt.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; the default method of deriving rulings by comparing new cases to established ones.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of departing from qiyas for a stronger evidence or public interest.
ثمن (thaman): Price, cash (dirhams and dinars) used as a medium of exchange.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why can the qadi sell the debtor's cash (dirhams/dinars) but not goods (urud)?
A) Because cash is indivisible and goods are divisible.
B) Because cash is a means (thaman) and goods have specific essence and form.
C) Because cash is less valuable than goods.
D) Because the creditor prefers cash over goods.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa permits the qadi to sell only the debtor's cash by istihsan, while the Sahibayn extend this to goods by qiyas – the distinction turns on whether the asset is a mere means (thaman) or an end in itself ('ayn).

Imprisonment of the Bankrupt Debtor for Contract Debts
Ruling on imprisonment of bankrupt debtor for contract debts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the types of debts for which a bankrupt debtor is imprisoned according to the Hanafi school and state the conditions for such imprisonment.

Core Idea
Imprisonment is permissible only for debts voluntarily undertaken by contract, such as mahr and kafalah, not for all debts.

This passage from Al-Hidayah discusses when a judge may imprison a bankrupt debtor. The key distinction is between debts that arise from contracts (like dower or guaranty) and those that arise from property exchanges (like price of goods). The judge has discretion to imprison only for contract debts when the debtor claims no assets and creditors request imprisonment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions for imprisonment
Note that the debtor must have no known wealth (or claims to have none) and the creditors must request imprisonment. The debt must be one that the debtor undertook by contract (التزمه بعقد).
The passage specifies debts like mahr (dower) and kafalah (guaranty) as examples.
2
Compare with the original text of al-Quduri
The commentary mentions that al-Hidayah omitted a part from al-Quduri that also included debts arising from property received, like the price of a sold item (ثمن المبيع) and loan repayment (بدل القرض). Understand that although many debts lead to imprisonment, the focus of this passage is on contract debts.
This shows the author's editorial choice; the omitted part is still valid law.
3
Note the judge's discretion
The ruling says 'the judge imprisons him' (حبسه الحاكم), indicating that the judge has the authority but it is not obligatory; it is at his discretion based on the request of creditors.
This is a mubah (permissible) action for the judge.

قوله فان لم يعرف للمفلس مال وطلب غرماء حبسه وهو يقول لا مال لي حبسه الحاكم في كل دين التزمه بعقد كالمهر والكفالة وقد ذكرنا هذا الفصل بوجوهه في كتاب ادب القاضى من هذا الكتاب فلا نعيدها الى ان قال وكذلك ان اقام البينة انه لا مال له يعنى خلى سبيله لوجوب النظرة الى الميسرة قوله فان لم يعرف ..... الخ اگر مفلس کا کچھ مال ظاہر نہ ہو اور قرض خواہ لوگ اس کو قید کرنے کی درخواست کریں۔ حالانکہ مدیون یہی کہتا ہے کہ میرے پاس کچھ مال نہیں ہے تو حاکم اس کو ہر ایسے قرضہ میں محبوس کرلے جس کا اس نے اپنے اوپر بذریعہ عقد التزام کیا ہو۔ جیسے مہر اور کفالت وغیرہ۔ تنبیہ... اس مقام پرمختصر القدوری اور بدا یہ متن کی اصل عبارت یوں تھی : وان لم يعرف للمفلس مال و طلب غرماء حبسه وهو يقول لا مال لى حبسه الحاكم في كل دين لزمه بدلا عن مال حصل فى يده كثمن المبيع و بدل القرض وفى كل دين التزمه بعقد كالمهر والكفالة اهـ لیکن اس مسئلہ کو ہدا یہ میں نقل کرتے وقت صاحب ہدایہ سے خط کشید و عبارت بمقتضاء بشریت کسی امر عارض سہو ونسیان و غیرہ کی وجہ سے ترک ہو گئی ۔ قوله الى ان قال ..... الخ - يہ لفظ قول سابق فان لم يعرف للمفلس مال سے متعلق ہے۔ یعنی امام قدوری نے مختصر میں كها فان لم يعرف للمفلس مال الى ان قال وكذلك ان اقام البيئة انه لا له مال اور عبارت یعنی علی سبیلہ صاحب ہدایہ کی طرف سے ہے۔ جس کا مقصد و کذالک ان اقام البينة انه لا مال له کی مراد کی تفسیر ہے اور لوجوب النظر الميسرة اس کی تعلیل ہے۔ پس صاحب ہدایہ نے یہاں اپنے اور قدوری کے کلام کو خلط کر دیا جو موجب تشویش ہو گیا۔ بہتر یہ تھا کہ الی ان قال کو وقد ذكرنا هذا الفضل اس سے پہلے ذکر کرتے یا لفظ الی ان قال کو بالکل ترک کر دیتے اور یوں کہتے قال و کذلک ان اقام البيئة جبکہ دیگر عام مواضع میں موصوف کی یہی عادت ہے۔ بہر کیف قول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر مفلس مذکور نے مبینہ قائم کر دیا تو اس کو چھوڑ دیا جائیگا۔ کیونکہ آسانی کے وقت تک مہلت دینا بحكم نص و ان كان ذو عسرة فنظرة الى ميسرة واجب ہے۔ فائدہ قید ہونے کے بعد ناداری پر بعینہ قائم کرنا تو بالا تفاق مقبول ہے۔ رہا یہ کہ اگر مفلس مذکور نے قید ہونے سے پہلے اپنی ناداری پر بینہ قائم کیا تو وہ بھی قبول کیا جائے گا یا نہیں؟ سو اس کی بابت دور و استیں ہیں۔ ایک یہ کہ قبول کیا جائے گا۔ شیخ ابو بکر محمد بن الفضل اس کا فتوی دیتے تھے۔ دوم یه که قبل از حس بدینہ مقبول نہ ہوگا۔ عام مشائخ اس روایت پر ہیں اور شمس الائمہ مرضی شرح ادب القاضی میں اس طرف گئے ہیں اور یہی بیج ہے۔
His saying: 'If no wealth is known for the bankrupt and the creditors request his imprisonment while he says I have no wealth, the judge imprisons him for every debt he has undertaken by contract, like mahr and guaranty. We have mentioned this chapter with its details in the Book of Adab al-Qadi from this book, so we will not repeat it until he said: And similarly if he proves that he has no wealth, meaning he is released, due to the obligation of respite until ease.' Commentary: 'His saying: If no wealth is known... etc. If the bankrupt's wealth is not apparent and the creditors request his imprisonment, while the debtor says I have no wealth, then the judge imprisons him for every debt that he has undertaken by contract, like mahr and guaranty. Note: The original text of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and the Bada'i' text was: "And if no wealth is known for the bankrupt and the creditors request his imprisonment while he says I have no wealth, the judge imprisons him for every debt that becomes binding in exchange for property that came into his hand, like the price of a sold item and the substitute of a loan, and for every debt he has undertaken by contract, like mahr and guaranty." However, when quoting this issue in al-Hidayah, the author inadvertently omitted the underlined phrase due to forgetfulness. His saying "until he said" – this phrase is related to the previous saying "if no wealth is known". That is, Imam Quduri said in Mukhtasar: "if no wealth is known for the bankrupt until he said: and similarly if he proves that he has no wealth." And the phrase "meaning he is released" is from Sahib al-Hidayah, which explains the meaning of "and similarly he proves that he has no wealth", and "due to the obligation of respite until ease" is its reasoning. So Sahib al-Hidayah mixed his own speech with Quduri's, causing confusion. It would have been better to put "until he said" before "and we have mentioned this chapter", or to omit "until he said" entirely and say "he said and similarly he proves", as is his usual practice in other places. Nevertheless, the meaning is that if the mentioned bankrupt proves (by evidence) his poverty, he will be released because granting respite until ease is obligatory by the text: "And if he is in difficulty, then respite until ease." Benefit: After imprisonment, proving poverty by evidence is accepted by consensus. However, whether it is accepted before imprisonment is a matter of dispute. One view: it will be accepted; Shaykh Abu Bakr ibn al-Fadl used to give fatwa accordingly. Second view: it will not be accepted before imprisonment; the majority of scholars follow this narration, and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi in his commentary on Adab al-Qadi inclined towards this, and this is correct.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage from the commentary discusses two main points: (1) The conditions under which a bankrupt debtor is imprisoned. The judge imprisons him for debts that he has voluntarily undertaken by contract, such as mahr (dower) and kafalah (guaranty). The text originally in al-Quduri also included debts for property received, like the price of goods sold or loan repayment, but al-Hidayah omitted that part. (2) If the debtor proves by evidence that he has no assets, he is released because of the Quranic command: 'And if he is in difficulty, then respite until ease' (Quran 2:280). After imprisonment, such proof is accepted unanimously. Before imprisonment, there is a difference: some accept it, but the majority view is that it is not accepted until after imprisonment, which is the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
بينة (bayyinah): Legal proof or evidence presented in court.
نظرة (nazrah): A period of time granted to the debtor to pay his debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, for which type of debt does the judge imprison the bankrupt debtor?
A) Any debt
B) Debts undertaken by contract
C) Only loans
D) Only tort debts

Key Takeaway
Imprisonment of a bankrupt debtor is permissible only for debts arising from voluntary contracts, subject to the debtor claiming no assets and creditors' request.

Release of the Bankrupt Debtor upon Proof of Poverty and Timing Dispute
Ruling on release with Quranic proof and intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on releasing a debtor who proves poverty, cite the Quranic proof, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the timing of accepting such evidence.

Core Idea
Release is wajib upon proof of poverty, but evidence is only accepted after imprisonment per the majority view.

This passage continues from the previous ruling and addresses the release of a bankrupt debtor. The proof is the Quranic verse commanding respite for the debtor in difficulty. A key intra-Hanafi dispute arises: is the debtor's evidence of poverty accepted before imprisonment or only after? The majority position, supported by Shams al-A'imma, is that it is not accepted before imprisonment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the proof for release
The commentator cites Quran 2:280 as the basis for the obligation of respite (nazrah). Release is wajib because the verse commands granting time until ease.
The imperative 'فنظرة' indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
2
Understand the consensus after imprisonment
The text states that after imprisonment, if the debtor proves poverty by evidence (bayyinah), release is accepted by consensus (بالاتفاق). This is straightforward.
3
Analyze the dispute on timing before imprisonment
Two views: 1) Some scholars like Shaykh Abu Bakr accept evidence before imprisonment. 2) The majority, and Shams al-A'imma, do not accept it before imprisonment, because the debtor may be concealing assets. The relied-upon fatwa is the latter.
The thamarah al-khilaf is whether the debtor avoids imprisonment or not.
4
Note the editorial issue in al-Hidayah
The commentator mentions that al-Hidayah mixed Quduri's text with his own, causing confusion in the flow. This is a textual note, but the legal ruling is clear.

The Skilled Debtor: Freedom to Earn and Repay
Ruling that a professional debtor is not prevented from working to earn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a skilled insolvent is not prevented from working, and explain the rationale considering both debtor and creditor.

Core Idea
A skilled debtor is not prevented from working because earning benefits both his family and his creditors.

This lesson addresses a practical scenario in Islamic commercial law: when a debtor becomes insolvent, can a creditor force him to stop working? The Hanafi school, as conveyed in the Hidayah, rules that a skilled professional debtor (muhtarif) is not to be prevented from pursuing his trade. The reasoning balances the debtor's need to support his family with the creditor's right to eventually recover the debt from surplus earnings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and the ruling
The text refers to a muhtarif (skilled professional) who is insolvent. The ruling is that he is not to be prevented (قابو نہیں دیا جائے گا) from working.
The debtor is allowed to continue his trade.
2
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi scholars held that the debtor should be prevented from working, but the majority (Imam al-Khassaf, the author of Hidayah) say he should not. The text endorses this majority view.
Hidayah says 'هوا صحیح' (this is correct).
3
Examine cross-madhhab agreement
Imam al-Shafi'i's more correct saying (اصح قول) also agrees that the debtor is not prevented.
Consensus across schools strengthens the ruling.
4
Analyse the rationale (talil)
The ruling considers both sides: the debtor earns maintenance for his family, and the creditor gets the surplus from earnings to pay off the debt.
The rationale uses the principle of balancing interests (رعایت جانبین).
5
Apply to a modern scenario
Consider a carpenter who owes money. He should be allowed to continue carpentry; creditors cannot force him to stop, as his work benefits both parties.
This prevents distress and promotes repayment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله والمحترف ...... الخ - اگر مفلس مذکور کوئی پیشہ ور آدمی ہو تو اس کو کام کرنے پر قابو نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ تا کہ وہ تنگدل ہو کر بعجلت اداء قرض پر آمادہ ہو۔ بقول امام خصاف اصبح یہی ہے اور صاحب ہدایہ نے ہوا صحیح کہہ کر ہمارے بعض مشائخ کے قول سے احتراز کیا ہے کہ حرفت و اکتساب سے نہیں روکا جائے گا۔ امام شافعی کا بھی اصح قول یہی ہے۔ کیونکہ اس میں جانبین کی رعایت ہے۔ مدیون کی رعایت تو یہ ہے کہ وہ کمائی سے اپنے اہل و عیال کا نفقہ حاصل کرے گا اور قرض خواہ کی رعایت یہ ہے کہ اس کی کمائی سے جو فاضل ہو گا وہ ادا با قرض میں صرف کر ے گا۔
His statement: 'And the professional...' If the mentioned insolvent is a professional person, he will not be controlled from working, so that he may become willing to pay off the debt quickly. According to Imam al-Khassaf, this is the correct view. And the author of Hidayah said 'this is correct' to avoid the saying of some of our scholars that he should be prevented from craft and earning. Imam al-Shafi'i's more correct saying is also this. Because it takes into consideration both sides: consideration of the debtor is that he will earn maintenance for his family, and consideration of the creditor is that the surplus from his earnings will be used to pay the debt.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage discusses a skilled debtor (muhtarif). The ruling is that he should not be prevented from working. The reason is to keep him from becoming distressed and unwilling to repay. Imam al-Khassaf affirms this as the correct view. The author of Hidayah endorses it, distinguishing it from some Hanafi scholars who would prevent him from working. Imam al-Shafi'i's more correct view is also that he is not prevented. The wisdom is that it serves both parties: the debtor supports his family, and the creditor gets paid from the surplus.

Key Terms
محترف (muhtarif): A skilled professional or craftsman.
کسب (kasb): Earning; acquisition of wealth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is a skilled insolvent not prevented from working?
A) To punish him by making him work hard.
B) To allow him to earn for his family and pay his debts.
C) Because he is not required to work.
D) Because his creditors do not want him to work.

Key Takeaway
A skilled debtor is allowed to work because it benefits both his family and his creditors.

Dispute over Seller's Rights upon Buyer's Insolvency
Inter-madhhab dispute on seller's rights upon buyer's insolvency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on seller's rights upon buyer's insolvency and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
The seller is an ordinary creditor; insolvency does not create a right to reclaim specific goods.

When a buyer is declared bankrupt (muflis) and the seller finds his exact goods in the buyer's possession, a critical legal question arises: does the seller have priority to reclaim his goods, or is he equal to other creditors? This lesson examines the Hanafi position and the Shafi'i counter-argument, focusing on the proofs and reasoning each school employs.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: the seller is equal to other creditors and has no right of rescission. Note the condition that bankruptcy occurred after the buyer took possession.
The ruling is found in the matn: the seller is 'equal to the other creditors'.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam Shafi'i, along with Malik and others, holds that the seller has the right to rescind the contract and reclaim his goods upon the buyer's insolvency.
The opponent's view is based on a hadith and an analogy to the seller's inability to deliver.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i proof: the hadith 'Whoever finds his goods with a bankrupt person has more right to it' and the qiyas comparing the buyer's inability to pay to the seller's inability to deliver.
The Shafi'i qiyas argues that the contract of exchange requires equality, so if one party cannot perform, the other may rescind.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi counter-argument: the Shafi'i hadith is weak (majhul al-isnad), and the qiyas is invalid because the buyer's inability to pay does not stem from a contractual obligation to deliver a specific item—the debt is in the dhimma.
The Hanafi proof includes a mursal hadith from Darqutni: 'it is his property among his creditors.'
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Note the practical consequence: under Hanafi law, the bankrupt's assets are distributed proportionally; under Shafi'i law, the seller can reclaim his goods. The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
This difference affects how creditors are treated in bankruptcy proceedings.

لقوله عليه السلام لا تاخذ الاسلمک او راس مالک
پس مال عین کو دین کا حکم دے دیا گیا۔ تحرزاً عن الاستبدال دلیل کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ جو امر بذریعہ عقد مستحق ہے وہ ایسا وصف ہے جو ثابت فی الذمہ ہے۔ اودین کی ادائیگی واجب ہے جو وصف کے ذریعہ سے نہیں ہو سکتی اسلئے شارع نے عین شی کو اس کا بدل قرار دے دیا۔ پس جب اس نے بدلہ میں مین شیء پر قبضہ کر لیا تو ان دونوں میں مبادلہ تحقیق ہو گیا۔ بایں معنی کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک کیلئے دوسرے کے ذمہ ایک وصف ثابت ہو گیا اور قضاء دین کے سلسلہ میں تحقق مبادلہ ہی حقیقت ہے تو اس کا اعتبار ضروری ہوگا۔

فائدہ . ہماری روایتی دلیل سنن دار قطنی کی حدیث ابوہریرہ ہے۔
ایما رجل باع سلعةً فادركها عند رجل قد افلس فهو ماله بين غرمائه
یہ حدیث گومرسل ہے ۔ مگر حدیث مرسل ہمارے نزدیک حجت ہے۔ ویسے امام خصاف اور امام رازی نے اس کو مسند بھی کیا ہے اور معنی یہ ہیں اس کو بیع کے طور پر دیا تھا اور ہنوز بیع تام نہیں ہوئی تھی ۔ حدیث کے الفاظ فادر کھا عند رجل قد افلس میں اس کی طرف اشارہ موجود ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ ذکر نہیں کیا کہ اس کو مشتری کے پاس پایا جو مفلس ہوا ہے۔
Translation: Whoever becomes bankrupt and with him is someone else's specific item that he had bought from him, then the owner of the item is equal to the other creditors. Imam Shafi'i says: The judge should place interdiction on the buyer at the request of the seller, then the seller will have the option to rescind. Because the buyer became unable to pay the price, so he made the right of rescission obligatory, just as if the seller becomes unable to deliver the sold item, and this is because this is a contract of exchange whose requirement is equality, and it becomes like salam. Our proof is that insolvency renders one unable to deliver the specific item, but this inability is not from the contract, so the right of rescission is not established on its basis. The obligation is a description in the dhimma, i.e., a debt, and by taking possession of the specific property, exchange between the two is realized. This is the reality, so it must be considered. Except in a place where there is difficulty, like salam, because there replacement is impossible. So the specific item is given the ruling of a debt. And Allah knows best. Commentary: His saying 'and whoever becomes bankrupt...' etc. A person is declared bankrupt and in his possession is someone else's specific item that he had bought from him, then according to us that person will be an equal partner with the other creditors, provided that the bankruptcy occurred after taking possession. Imam Zuhri, Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz, Qadi Shurayh, Ibn Jurayj, Ibrahim al-Nakhai, Ibn Shirmah also held this view, and Muhammad ibn Sirin used to give fatwa accordingly. His saying 'and al-Shafi'i said...' etc. Imam Shafi'i says that person is entitled to his own item. So at the seller's request, the judge will compel the buyer, and then the seller can rescind the contract and take his item. Imam Malik, Ahmad, al-Awza'i, Ishaq, Abu Thawr, Ibn al-Mundhir also held this view, and it is also narrated from Uthman and Abu Hurairah. The hadith of Samura ibn Jundub: 'Whoever finds his goods with a bankrupt person specifically, he has more right to it.' But in its chain, Ibrahim is a narrator who, according to Abu Hatim, is not reliable. The objection: Abu Dawud al-Tayalisi narrated from Abi Dhi'b, from Abu al-Mu'tamir, from Umar ibn Khalid: He said: We came to Abu Hurairah regarding a companion of ours who became bankrupt, and a man found his specific goods. Abu Hurairah said: This is what the Messenger of Allah ruled regarding whoever becomes bankrupt or dies and a man finds his specific goods, he has more right to it, unless the man leaves enough to pay. Response: Shaykh Abd al-Haqq mentioned in al-Ahkam the saying of Imam Abu Dawud: Who accepts this? Who is Abu al-Mu'tamir? i.e., he is not known. We do not know who he is, nor have we heard of him except in this hadith. Imam Tahawi says: In al-Ishraf it is: a hadith of unknown chain. His saying 'because the buyer's inability...' etc. This is Imam Shafi'i's analogical proof: the buyer became unable to pay the price, so from this aspect the seller obtains the right of rescission, just as if the seller becomes unable to deliver the sold item, the right of rescission is obtained. The reason is that sale is a contract of exchange whose requirement is equality. So just as in the case of the seller's inability the buyer has the right of rescission, similarly in the case of the buyer's inability the seller has the right of rescission. So this becomes like the contract of salam: if the subject matter becomes unavailable on the market, the seller of salam has the option to rescind. His saying 'and our proof is that insolvency...' etc. Our proof is that insolvency causes the inability to deliver the specific item, although here no property became obligatory through the contract. So by virtue of insolvency, the seller will not obtain the right of rescission. And by virtue of the contract, only a right to something that is a description in the buyer's dhimma is established, i.e., the debt, and that is the cash price. And when the seller takes possession of the specific property, the exchange between the seller and buyer becomes realized. And the real meanings are not [other], so they must be considered, except in a situation where exchange is impossible, like in salam, because there replacement is forbidden. Due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Do not take [the property] as salam or your capital.' So the specific property is given the ruling of a debt, as a precaution against replacement. The summary of the proof is that what is owed by virtue of the contract is a description that is established in the dhimma, and repayment of a debt is obligatory, which cannot be done through a description. Therefore, the Lawgiver made the specific thing its substitute. So when he took possession of the specific thing as a substitute, exchange between them was realized. In the sense that for each of them, a description becomes established in the dhimma of the other. And in the matter of debt repayment, the realization of exchange is the reality, so it must be considered. Benefit: Our transmitted proof is the hadith of Abu Hurairah in Sunan al-Darqutni: 'Any man who sells a commodity and finds it with a man who has become bankrupt, it is his property among his creditors.' This hadith is mursal, but a mursal hadith is evidence according to us. Moreover, Imam al-Khassaf and Imam al-Razi have also narrated it as musnad. And the meaning is that he had given it as a sale, and the sale had not yet been completed. The words of the hadith 'fadrakaha inda rajulin qad aflasa' indicate this, because it is not mentioned that he found it with the buyer who was bankrupt.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the rights of a seller when the buyer becomes bankrupt (muflis) before paying the price, and the seller finds his exact goods in the buyer's possession. The text presents the Hanafi position, the Shafi'i position, and the Hanafi response.

The Hanafi ruling, as stated in the matn: the seller is merely an equal partner with other creditors; he has no priority to reclaim his specific goods. This is the position of the Hanafi school and is also attributed to several early authorities including Imam Zuhri and Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz. The Shafi'i position, endorsed by Malik, Ahmad, and others, is that the seller has the right to rescind the contract and take back his goods upon the buyer's insolvency, based on the hadith 'Whoever finds his goods with a bankrupt person has more right to it.'

The Hanafi objection to the Shafi'i proof is that the hadith cited by Shafi'i is weak in chain (majhul al-isnad) due to unknown narrators. They also point out contradictions. The Hanafi's own transmitted proof is a hadith from Abu Hurairah in Sunan al-Darqutni: 'Any man who sells a commodity and finds it with a man who has become bankrupt, it is his property among his creditors.' Though mursal, the Hanafis accept mursal hadith as evidence.

The core Hanafi rational argument is that insolvency causes inability to deliver the specific item, but this inability is not a contractual obligation; the contract only creates a debt (dayn) in the dhimma. The specific item is not the subject of the debt; rather, the debt is the price. Thus, the seller cannot claim specific performance. He is only entitled to a share in the proceeds from the sale of the buyer's assets. By taking possession of the specific goods, the seller is actually receiving payment of the debt in kind, which is valid only if the other creditors agree, because all are equal. The exception is the salam contract, where the specific item is treated as a debt due to impossibility of substitution.

Thus, the Hanafi position is that the seller is an ordinary creditor, and the goods are part of the bankrupt's estate to be distributed proportionally among all creditors. This is the mufta bihi (relied upon) ruling in the Hanafi school, as established in the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
مفلس (muflis): A person who is declared bankrupt by a judge due to inability to pay debts.
حجر (hajr): Judicial interdiction restricting a person's financial transactions due to insolvency or other reasons.
فسخ (faskh): Rescission or cancellation of a contract, here the sale, allowing the seller to take back his goods.
دين (dayn): A debt that is an obligation in the dhimma (liability), not a specific tangible item.
عين ('ayn): A specific tangible good that can be identified and possessed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens to a seller who finds his specific goods in the possession of a buyer who has been declared bankrupt?
A) The seller has the right to rescind the contract and reclaim his goods.
B) The seller is equal to other creditors and shares in the bankrupt's assets proportionally.
C) The seller has no claim at all.
D) The seller can recover his goods if the buyer agrees.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a seller is an equal creditor with no right to reclaim specific goods from a bankrupt buyer; the debt is in the dhimma, not tied to the item.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
The Nature of Idhn in Hanafi Fiqh: Definition and Dispute
Defining idhn and its legal nature with a comparative dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of idhn, explain why it is not agency, and apply the rule that restrictions on a permitted slave are invalid.

Core Idea
Idhn removes a barrier; the slave acts by his own capacity, not as an agent.

In this lesson, we examine the concept of idhn (permission) as it appears in the Hanafi legal tradition, specifically in the context of the ma'dhun (permitted slave). The passage from Al-Hidayah and its commentaries defines idhn both linguistically and legally, and addresses a key dispute: does idhn make the slave an agent, or does it simply remove the interdiction so that the slave transacts on his own behalf? Understanding this distinction is crucial for grasping the Hanafi position on the scope of the slave's authority to trade.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic definition
Examine the claim that idhn means 'information' (i'lam) and the critique from lexicons that only 'adhan' has that meaning. Note the preferred view: idhn is the opposite of hajr (prohibition).
See the discussion on the authority of Khahrazada in al-Mabsut.
2
Analyse the legal definition
The legal definition is fakk al-hajr wa isqat al-haqq (removal of interdiction and dropping of a right). Understand that the right is the master's right to prevent the slave from transacting, and it is dropped only for commercial matters.
The scope excludes gifts and manumission.
3
Determine the scope of permission
Idhn is limited to commercial transactions (tijarah). The slave is not permitted to make gratuitous transfers or free slaves without additional permission.
This limitation is part of the definition.
4
Compare with the opposing view
Imam Zufar, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad consider idhn as appointment as an agent (wakalah). Understand their reasoning: analogy with agency because the master gives permission to trade on his behalf.
The Hanafi response: idhn removes the prohibition; the slave's own capacity is sufficient.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence
If the master restricts permission to a specific time or trade, the opposing schools validate the restriction; Hanafis do not, because after removal of interdiction the slave acts by his own capacity and cannot be restricted.
This difference is the thamarah al-khilaf.

اذن کا لغوی اور شرعی معنیٰ
الاذن هو الاعلام لغة وفى الشرع فك الحجر واسقاط الحق عن
ترجمہ اذن لغت میں بمعنی آگاہ کرنا ہے اور شرع میں حجر دور کرنا اور حق ساقط کرنا ہے ہمارے نزدیک ۔ تشریح... قوله كتاب ..... الخ كتاب الماذون کو کتاب الحجر کے بعد اسلئے لائے ہیں کہ اذن سبقت حجر کو چاہتی ہے یعنی مقتضائے اذن یہ ہے کہ جس تصرف سے پہلے روک دیا گیا تھا اب اس کی اجازت دے دی گئی۔
قوله الاذن هو الاعلام.... الخ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اذن الغنہ بمعنی اعلام ہے یعنی اطلاع کر دینا اور بتا دینا۔ اکثر کتب فقہیہ میں بھی یہی مذکور ہے لیکن صاحب نتائج کہتے ہیں کہ لغت کی متداول کتابوں میں کہیں بھی یہ مذکور نہیں کہ اذن لفظ بمعنی اعلام ہے بلکہ ان میں تو لفظ اذان بمعنی اعلام آیا ہے۔ پس فقہاء کی تفسیر مبنی بر تسامح ہے۔ گویا لفظ اذن جو اذن (س) له في الشئ سے ہے بمعنی اجازت دینا اور مباح کرنا جیسا کہ قاموس وغیرہ میں مصرح ہے۔ اس معنی کی تعبیر وہ اسلام سے کرتے ہیں بایں معنی کہ اباحت کے لئے عادۃ اعلام لازم ہے صاحب نہایہ کے کلام میں اس کی طرف اشارہ بھی ہے حيث قال : ههنا يحتاج الى بيان الاذن لغةً وشرعاً. ثم قال اما اللغه فالاذن في الشئ رفع المانع لمن هو محجور عنه و اعلام باطلاقه فيما حجر عنه من اذن له في الشئ اذنا اه.
پھر علامہ زیلعی نے جو تبیین میں کہا ہے والا ذن فی اللغة الاعلام ومنه الاذان وهو الاعلام مدخول الوقت اس طرح صاحب بدائع نے جو کہا ہے "لان الاذن هو الاعلام قال الله تعالى و اذان من الله ورسولہ "یہ تو بالکل ہی بعید ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کا مدار اذن اور اذان کے اتحاد پر ہے۔ حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہے پس اذن لغوی کی بات قرین قیاس وہ ہے جو شیخ الاسلام خواہر زادہ نے مبسوط میں ذکر کیا ہے کہ اذن لغۂ ضد حجر ہے۔ حجر کے معنی منع کرنا اور روکنا ہے اور اؤں کے معنی اس منع اور روکنے کو اٹھا دینا ہے۔ قوله وفی الشرع .... الخ را اصطلاح شرع میں اذن فک حجر و اسقاط حق کو کہتے ہیں یعنی بچہ کم سنی کی وجہ سے اور غلام رقیت کی وجہ سے جو ممنوع التصرف تھا ان کو تصرف کی اجازت دے دینا۔ فک حجر سے اطلاق حجر مطلقاً مراد نہیں بلکہ صرف امور تجارت کا اطلاق مراد ہے کیونکہ عبد ماذون کے لئے تبرع و اعتاق اور تکفیر بالمال کی اجازت نہیں ہوتی۔ اسقاط حق میں حق سے مراد حق آتا ہے جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جب آقا نے اپنے غلام کو تجارت کی اجازت دے دی تو اس کے جس حق کی وجہ سے غلام ممنوع التصرف تھا اس نے اجازت دے کر اپنے اس حق کو ساقط کر دیا۔ ہدایہ، عنایہ کفایہ وغیرہ سب میں یہی مذکوہ ہے صاحب تنویر و صاحب اصلاح و ایضاح نے کہا ہے کہ حق سے مراد حق منع ہے نہ کہ صرف حق آقا کیونکہ اس صورت میں اذن صرف غلام کو شامل ہوگا نہ کہ صغیر کو ۔ حالانکہ اذن غلام اورصغیر دونوں کو شامل ہے۔ مگر آفندی نے تکملہ میں کئی وجوہ سے تردید کی ہے۔

عندة
دنا کی قید کے ذریعہ امام زفر اور امام شافعی اور احمد کے قول سے احتراز ہے کہ ان کے نزدیک اذن کا مطلب وکیل کرنا اور نائب بنانا ہے۔ اس اختلاف کا ثمر یہ ہے کہ اگر آقا نے اذن کو کسی معین وقت یا کسی خاص قسم کی تجارت کے ساتھ مقید کیا تو ان حضرات کے یہاں تقیید صحیح ہوگی اور غلام اس کے خلاف نہ کر سکے گا ۔ ہمارے ہاں صحیح نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ انفکاک حجر کے بعد غلام اپنی اہلیت کے سبب سے تصرف کرتا ہے تو اذن اور تصرف نہ کسی وقت کے ساتھ مقید ہوگا اور نہ کسی خاص قسم کی تجارت کے ساتھ مخصوص ۔ اذن کے بعد غلام اپنی اہلیت سے تصرف کر سکتا ہے
The Book of the Permitted Slave. The linguistic and legal meaning of idhn: Idhn is information linguistically, and legally it is the removal of interdiction and dropping of a right. Commentary: ... The chapter is placed after the chapter of interdiction because permission requires prior interdiction. The author of Hidayah says idhn means information. However, the author of Nata'ij says the lexicons do not support this; rather, 'adhan' means information. The correct view is that idhn is the opposite of hajr (prohibition), as stated by Khahrazada. Legally, idhn is the removal of interdiction and dropping of the master's right, limited to commercial transactions. There is a difference: Imam Zufar, Shafi'i, and Ahmad consider idhn as appointment of agency, so it can be restricted to time or type. In our school, it cannot be restricted because after removal of interdiction, the slave acts by his own capacity.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage is a definition and discussion of the term 'idhn' (permission) as used in Hanafi fiqh, specifically Kitab al-Ma'dhun. The author begins by presenting the linguistic and legal definitions. Linguistically, idhn is often said to mean 'information' (i'lam), but this is refuted by citing that the lexicons only record 'adhan' (call to prayer) with that meaning. The preferred view is that idhn means 'removal of prohibition' (raf' al-mani'), as stated by Khahrazada in al-Mabsut. Legally, idhn is defined as the removal of interdiction (fakk al-hajr) and the dropping of a right (isqat al-haqq). The right here is the master's right to prevent the slave from transacting, and it is dropped only for commercial matters, not for gifts or manumission. The passage then discusses a debate: Imam Zufar, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad hold that idhn is analogous to agency (wakalah), meaning if the master restricts permission to a specific time or trade, it is valid. In the Hanafi school, however, idhn is not agency; it is the removal of a barrier, so after permission the slave acts by his own legal capacity (ahliyyah) and cannot be restricted. The practical consequence (thamar al-khilaf) is that Hanafis do not allow such restrictions, while the opposing schools do.

Key Terms
الإذن (al-idhn): Linguistically: information (i'lam). Legally: removal of interdiction and dropping of a right (fakk al-hajr wa isqat al-haqq), specifically for commercial transactions.
الحجر (al-hajr): Interdiction; legal prohibition from transacting due to minority or slavery.
الوكالة (al-wakalah): Agency; appointment of another to act on one's behalf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a master gives permission to his slave for trade but restricts it to buying only textiles, what is the ruling?
A) The restriction is valid and the slave cannot buy other items.
B) The restriction is invalid and the slave may buy any trade goods.
C) The permission becomes void if restricted.
D) The slave becomes an agent restricted to textiles only.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, idhn is the removal of interdiction, not the appointment as agent, so any restrictions on the scope of permission are invalid.

Legal Capacity of the Permitted Slave After Permission
Explaining that the permitted slave transacts by his own capacity after permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the permitted slave transacts by his own capacity and distinguish this from acting as an agent.

Core Idea
The permitted slave transacts for himself, not as an agent; his latent capacity is unlocked by the master's permission.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a key question in Hanafi fiqh: when a master permits his slave to trade, does the slave act as an agent for the master or for himself? The answer hinges on the nature of legal capacity (ahliyyah). We will explore how the slave's inherent capacity, once the master's right is removed, makes him the principal in his own transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
State the exact ruling: after permission, the slave transacts for himself (linafsihi) by his own capacity (bi-ahliyyatihi). Note that this applies to the 'abd ma'dhun (permitted slave).
The ruling is a clear statement of the Hanafi position.
2
Analyze the reasoning (ta'lil)
Break down the author's proof: the rukn of a transaction is speech (with intellect and tongue) and the place is the dhimma (legal personality). Both remain in the slave despite slavery. The prohibition was only due to the master's right; permission removes that barrier, allowing the slave's own capacity to operate.
The passage uses the term 'mahjur' (prohibited) to indicate a temporary restriction, not a removal of capacity.
3
Address the counterargument
The passage includes a hypothetical question: if the slave lacks full capacity for ownership (milk al-raqaba), how can he transact? The answer distinguishes between full ownership and possessory ownership (milk al-yadd). The slave is eligible for milk al-yadd, as evidenced by the mukatab (slave on contract of manumission) who also possesses earnings.
This distinction is crucial to understanding the Hanafi view that the slave transacts for himself.
4
Contrast with the opposing view
Note that other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider the slave an agent, so ownership goes to the master. The Hanafi response relies on the retention of personal capacity and the concept of milk al-yadd.
This step highlights the practical difference: who owns the property acquired by the slave.

سوال عبد ماذون تو حکم تصرف یعنی ملک کے لحاظ سے عدیم الا ہلیت ہے۔ پس وہ نفس تصرف کا اہل نہیں ہونا چاہیے کیونکہ شرعی تصرفات ان کے احکام ہی کی وجہ سے مقصود ہوتے ہیں اور غلام تصرف کا اہل نہیں ہے تو اس کے سبب کا بھی اہل نہیں ہو گا۔ جوار با حکم تصرف ملک ید ہے اور رقیق اس کا اہل ہے چنانچہ قیام رقیت کے باوجود مکاتب کو ملک پید کا استحقاق ہوتا ہے۔
And the slave after that transacts for himself by his capacity, because after slavery he remained eligible for transaction by his speaking tongue and discerning intellect, and his prohibition from transaction was due to the master's right, because his transaction is not customary except as a cause for debt to attach to his neck or his earnings, and that is the master's wealth, so permission is necessary so that his right is not voided without his consent. Commentary: ... After the master drops his right, the slave acts for himself by his own competence, not as a proxy. The pillar of transaction is his speech, which is valid by shariah, and the place of transaction is his dhimma, which can assume obligations. These are not lost by slavery. The question: The permitted slave is lacking in capacity for ownership, so he should not be eligible for the transaction itself. Answer: The ruling of transaction is possession of ownership (milk al-yadd), and the slave is eligible for that, as the mukatab deserves milk al-yadd.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the legal capacity of the permitted slave (al-'abd al-ma'dhun). It states that after permission, the slave transacts for himself by his own inherent capacity (ahliyyah). The reasoning: the essential elements of a transaction (rukn) are speech (with speaking tongue and discerning intellect) and a dhimma (legal personality) capable of assuming obligations. Slavery does not remove these; it only creates a prohibition due to the master's right over the slave's neck and earnings. Permission removes that prohibition, allowing the slave's latent capacity to operate. The commentary then addresses a question: if the slave lacks full capacity for ownership (milk al-raqaba), how can he transact? The answer distinguishes between ownership of property (milk al-raqaba) and possessory ownership (milk al-yadd). The slave is eligible for milk al-yadd, as seen in the case of a mukatab (slave not yet fully free) who is also entitled to possess earnings. Thus, the slave's transactions are valid and he acquires ownership (milk) through them, subject to the master's right to collect debts from his earnings.

Key Terms
الأهلية (al-ahliyyah): Legal capacity; the qualification to perform acts and assume rights. Here, the slave retains ahliyyat al-tasarruf (capacity to transact) despite slavery.
ملك اليد (milk al-yadd): Possessory ownership; the right to possess and benefit from property, as distinct from full ownership (milk al-raqaba).
الذمة (al-dhimmah): Legal personality; the capacity to assume obligations and rights. The slave's dhimmah remains intact.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a master gives permission (idhn) to his slave for trade, the slave's transactions are:
A) For the master, as the slave is an agent.
B) For the slave himself, by his own capacity.
C) Void if the slave owns nothing.
D) Valid only if the master's right is not affected.

Key Takeaway
The permitted slave transacts by his own capacity, not as an agent, and acquires possessory ownership (milk al-yadd) for himself.

Nature of Permission for the Slave Trader: Relinquishment vs Agency
Explains the nature of slave permission and its rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that permission for a slave to trade is a relinquishment of the master's right to interdict and apply the resulting rulings (no time limitation, no master liability, implied permission by silence).

Core Idea
Permission is not agency—it is dropping the right to block the slave's inherent capacity.

This lesson delves into the foundational distinction between the Hanafi and other schools regarding the nature of a master's permission for his slave to trade. Understanding this difference is crucial because it determines several practical rulings: whether the permission can be time-bound, who bears liability for the slave's debts, and whether silence implies consent. The Hidayah's commentary makes a strong rational case for the Hanafi view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed nature of permission
State the two competing views: Hanafi says permission is isqat al-haqq (relinquishment of the right to interdict); other schools (Zufar, Shafi'i, Ahmad) say it is wakalah (agency).
This is the central ikhtilaf.
2
Follow the Hanafi proof (dalil aqli)
Trace the reasoning: the slave retains full legal capacity (ahliyah) for transactions despite slavery; slavery only gives the master a right over the slave's neck and earnings. Permission removes that barrier, freeing the slave's inherent capacity to act for himself.
The proof is rational, based on the nature of capacity and the master's right.
3
Derive the practical effects (thamarah al-khilaf)
From the Hanafi view, deduce that permission cannot be time-bound (since relinquishments are not time-bound), the master is not liable for the slave's debts, and implied permission via silence is valid (since the rational for interdiction is to prevent harm to others, and silence indicates consent).
Contrast with the opposing view which leads to opposite results.
4
Address objections and confirm the Hanafi position
Consider two objections: (1) if permission is relinquishment, how can the master later re-interdict? (2) how can inference be drawn from a definition? The commentary resolves these: the master's right is continuous, so he may re-interdict for the future; inference is from subsidiary rulings, not from the definition itself.
This reinforces the consistency of the Hanafi position.

Source Text

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو بدان جلد ۱۲ دنا کی قید کے ذریعہ امام زفر اور امام شافعی اور احمد کے قول سے احتراز ہے کہ ان کے نزدیک اذن کا مطلب وکیل کرنا اور نائب بنانا ہے۔ اس اختلاف کا ثمر یہ ہے کہ اگر آقا نے اذن کو کسی معین وقت یا کسی خاص قسم کی تجارت کے ساتھ مقید کیا تو ان حضرات کے یہاں تقیید صحیح ہوگی اور غلام اس کے خلاف نہ کر سکے گا ۔ ہمارے ہاں صحیح نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ انفکاک حجر کے بعد غلام اپنی اہلیت کے سبب سے تصرف کرتا ہے تو اذن اور تصرف نہ کسی وقت کے ساتھ مقید ہوگا اور نہ کسی خاص قسم کی تجارت کے ساتھ مخصوص ۔ اذن کے بعد غلام اپنی اہلیت سے تصرف کر سکتا ہے
والعبد بعد ذلك يتصرف لنفسه باهليته لانه بعد الرق بقى اهلا للتصرف بلسانه الناطق وعقله المميز والحجارة عن التصرف لحق المولى لانه ما عهد الا موجبا لتعلق الدين برقبته او كسبه و ذلك مال المولى فلابد من اذنه كيلا يبطل حقه من غير رضاه
ترجمہ اور غلام اس اجازت کے بعد اپنے لئے اپنی اہلیت سے تصرف کرتا ہے کیونکہ وہ رقیت کے بعد تصرف کا اہل باقی رہا اپنی ناطق زبان اور عقل ممیز کے ساتھ اور تصرف سے اس کا مجور ہو نا حق آقا کی وجہ سے تھا کیونکہ غلام کا تصرف معہود نہیں۔ مگر اس کی گردن یا کمائی کے ساتھ تعلق دین کا موجب ہو کر حالانکہ یہ آقا کا مال ہے تو آقا کی اجازت ضروری ہے تا کہ اس کی رضاء کے بغیر اس کا حق باطل نہ
ہو جائے۔
تشریح قوله و العبد بعد ذالك الخ آقا کی طرف سے اسقاط حق کے بعد غلام برائے خود اپنی سابقہ اہلیت ولیاقت سے تصرف کرتا ہے گویا تصرف کی جو لیاقت اس کو پہلے حاصل تھی وہ اب کھل گئی پس اس کا تصرف اپنے لئے ہوگا نہ کہ اس کے آقا کے لئے بطریق توکیل دنیابت ، وجہ یہ ہے کہ غلام رقیت کے بعد بھی تصرفات کا اہل باقی رہتا ہے کیونکہ رکن تصرف تو اس کا کلام ہے جو شرعا معتبر ہے اس لئے کہ وہ زبان ناطق اور عقل ممیز کے ساتھ صادر ہوا ہے اور محل تصرف ایسا ذمہ ہے جو التزام حق کے قابل ہے اور یہ دونوں چیزیں رقیت سے فوت نہیں ہو جاتیں۔ کیونکہ ذمہ کا قابل التزام ہونا کرامات بشریہ میں سے ہے اور رقیت کی وجہ سے غلام بشر ہونے سے خارج نہیں ہوتا ۔ صرف اتنی بات ہے کہ اس کا تصرف سے محجور ہو نا حق آقا کی وجہ سے تھا۔ کیونکہ غلام کا تصرف اس طور پر معہود ہے کہ وہ اس کی گردن یا کمائی سے دین کے متعلق ہونے کا موجب ہو حالانکہ اس کی گردن اور کمائی آنا کا مال ہے تو آقا کی اجازت ضروری ہے تا کہ رضاء کے بغیر اس کا حق باطل نہ ہو جائے اور جب آقا نے اجازت دے دی تو وہ اپنے حق کے اسقاط سے خود راضی ہو گیا۔
سوال عبد ماذون تو حکم تصرف یعنی ملک کے لحاظ سے عدیم الا ہلیت ہے۔ پس وہ نفس تصرف کا اہل نہیں ہونا چاہیے کیونکہ شرعی تصرفات ان کے احکام ہی کی وجہ سے مقصود ہوتے ہیں اور غلام تصرف کا اہل نہیں ہے تو اس کے سبب کا بھی اہل نہیں ہو گا۔ جوار با حکم تصرف ملک ید ہے اور رقیق اس کا اہل ہے چنانچہ قیام رقیت کے باوجود مکاتب کو ملک پید کا استحقاق ہوتا ہے۔

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۲
۲۹۷
جو ذمہ داری ماذون کو لاحق ہو آقا کو لازم نہیں ہوگی
كتَابُ المادور
ولهذا لا يرجع بما لحقه من العهدة على المولى ولهذا لا يقبل التوقيت حتى لو اذن لعبده يوما كان ماذونا ابدا حتى يحجر عليه لان الاسقاطات لا تتوقت ثم الاذن كما يثبت بالصريح يثبت بالدلالة كما اذا رأى عبده يبيع ويشترى فسكت يصير ماذونا عندنا خلافا لزفر والشافعي ولا فرق بين ان يبيع عينا مملوكا للمولى او الاجنبى باذنه او بغير اذنه بيعا صحيحا او فاسدا لان كل من رآه يظنه ماذونا له فيها فيعاقده فيتضرر به لولم يكن ماذونا له ولو لم يكن المولى راضيا به لمنعه دفعا للضرر عنهم
ترجمہ اس لئے جو ذمہ داری اس کو لاحق ہو وہ آقا پر عائد نہیں ہوتی اور اسی لئے اجازت توقیت کو قبول نہیں کرتی ۔ یہاں تک کہ اگر غلام کو ایک روز کی اجازت دی تو وہ ہمیشہ کے لئے مازون ہو جائے گا یہاں تک کہ اس کو مجبور کر دے۔ کیونکہ اسقاطات موقت نہیں ہوتے پھر اجازت جیسے صریح سے ثابت ہوتی ہے ایسے ہی دلالت سے بھی ثابت ہو جاتی ہے جیسے اگر اپنے غلام کو خرید و فروخت کرتے دیکھ کر خاموش رہا تو وہ ہمارے نزدیک مازون ہو جائے گا بر خلاف امام زفر و شافعی کے۔ اور اس میں کوئی فرق نہیں کہ وہ آقا کا مملوک مال بیچتا ہو یا کسی اجنبی کا۔ اجازت سے ہو یا بلا اجازت بھی صحیح ہو یا فاسد اس لئے کہ اس کو جو بھی دیکھے گا ماذون فی التجارت سمجھے گا اور اس سے معاملہ
کرے گا۔ پس اگر وہ ماذون نہ ہو تو ضر راٹھائے گا اور آقا اگر اس پر راضی نہ ہوتا تو لوگوں سے دفع ضرر کی خاطر اس کو روک دیتا تشریح قوله ولهذا لا يرجع ... الخ يقول سابق و العبد بعد ذالك يتصرف لنفسه باهليته" کی طرف راجی ہے۔ یعنی اجازت کے بعد غلام چونکہ اپنی لیاقت سے تصرف کرتا ہے اس لئے جو ذمہ داری اس کو لاحق ہو وہ آقا یر عائد نہیں ہوتی یعنی آقا اس کا ضامن نہیں ہوتا۔ اور اسی لئے کہ اذن ہمارے نزدیک اسقاط حق ہے۔ اجازت کسی وقت تک می رود نہیں ہوتی۔ حتی کہ اگر غلام کو ایک روز کے لئے تجارت کی اجازت دی تو وہ ہمیشہ کے لئے مازون ہو جائے گا یہاں تک کہ آقا اس کو مجبور کرے وجہ یہ ہے کہ اسقاطات کسی وقت کے ساتھ موقت نہیں ہوتے۔ سوال اگر اذن مذکور اسقاط ہو تو اسقاط کے بعد آقا کے لئے ولایت حجر نہیں ہونی چاہیے۔ کیونکہ وہ اپنا حق ساقط کر چکا اور جو چیز ساقط ہو جائے وہ عود نہیں کرتی۔ حالانکہ آقا اس کے بعد بھی حجر کر سکتا ہے۔ جواب ... ولایت حجر بقاء رقیت کے اعتبار سے ہے۔ پس اجازت کے بعد پھر حجر کرنے میں اس حق کے اسقاط سے رکنا ہے جو اس کو بلحاظ مستقبل حاصل ہے اس اعتبار سے نہیں ہے کہ ساقط عود کر آیا۔ سوالف حجر اور اسقاط حق تو حیز تعریف میں مذکور ہے۔ حيث قال : وفی الشرع فك الحجر و اسقاط الحق‘ پھر اس پر استدلال کیسے درست ہوا۔ جواب استدلال مذکور نفس تعریف پر نہیں ہے یہاں تک کہ یہ اعتراض وارد ہو کہ تعریف استدلال کو قبول نہیں کرتی ۔ کیونکہ تعریف از قبیل تصورات ہے اور تصور کا اکتساب تصدیق سے نہیں ہوتا بلکہ استدلال حکم ضمنی پر ہے۔ "كان يقال هذا التعريف صحيح هذا التعريف مطابق لاصولنا اور ظاہر ہے کہ یہ احکام تصدیقات ہیں جن پر استدلال کیا جاسکتا ہے۔
Chapter of the Ma'dhun (Permitted Slave). By restricting [the permission] through time, there is avoidance of the statement of Imam Zufar, Imam Shafi'i, and Ahmad, because according to them the meaning of permission is appointing as agent and representative. The fruit of this difference is that if the master restricts the permission to a specific time or a specific type of trade, according to those scholars the restriction is valid and the slave cannot act contrary to it. According to us it will not be valid. Because after the removal of interdiction, the slave acts by virtue of his own competency, so permission and action are not restricted to a time nor specific to a type of trade. After permission, the slave can act with his competency. And the slave after that acts for himself by his competency, because after slavery he remained qualified for transaction with his speaking tongue and discerning intellect, and his being prevented from transaction was due to the right of the master, because his transaction is not customary except as a cause for the attachment of debt to his neck or his earnings, and that is the property of the master, so his permission is necessary so that his right is not invalidated without his consent. Translation: After this permission, the slave acts for himself with his competency, because after slavery he remained qualified for transaction with his speaking tongue and discerning intellect, and his being prevented from transaction was due to the right of the master, because the slave's transaction is not customary except as a cause for the attachment of debt to his neck or his earnings, while this is the master's property, so the master's permission is necessary so that his right is not invalidated without his consent. Commentary on 'and the slave after that...': After the master's relinquishment of right, the slave acts on his own behalf with his previous competency and capability, as if the capability for transaction that he possessed earlier has now been opened. So his transaction is for himself, not for his master as agency or representation. The reason is that the slave remains qualified for transactions even after slavery, because the pillar of transaction is his speech, which is legally valid because it is expressed with a speaking tongue and discerning intellect, and the locus of transaction is a dhimmah that is capable of undertaking obligations, and these two things are not lost due to slavery, because the capacity of the dhimmah to undertake obligations is part of human nobility, and due to slavery the slave does not cease to be a human. The only point is that his being prevented from transaction was due to the master's right, because the slave's transaction is customary in a way that it causes debt to attach to his neck or his earnings, while his neck and earnings are the master's property, so the master's permission is necessary so that his right is not invalidated without his consent. When the master has given permission, he has consented to the relinquishment of his right. Question: The authorized slave, from the perspective of the ruling of transaction (meaning ownership), is devoid of competency. So he should not be qualified for the transaction itself, because legal transactions are intended for their rulings, and the slave is not qualified for transaction, so he would not be qualified for its cause. Answer: By 'ruling of transaction' is meant ownership of acquisition, and the slave is qualified for it, even though the slave retains ownership of acquisition, as a mukatab is entitled to ownership of acquisition. ... Whatever liability befalls the ma'dhun, it will not be binding on the master. Chapter of the Ma'dhun: Therefore, what befalls him of liability does not revert to the master, and therefore permission does not accept time limitation, such that if he permitted his slave for one day, he is permanently permitted until he re-interdicts him, because relinquishments are not time-bound. Then, permission is established by explicit statement as well as by implication, as when he sees his slave buying and selling and remains silent, he becomes a ma'dhun according to us, contrary to Zufar and al-Shafi'i. There is no difference whether he sells an article owned by the master or by a stranger, with permission or without permission, a valid sale or an invalid one, because everyone who sees him thinks he is authorized for trade and contracts with him, and he would be harmed if he were not authorized. And if the master were not pleased with it, he would stop him to prevent harm from them. Translation: Therefore, whatever liability befalls him does not revert to the master, and for this reason permission does not accept time limitation, to the extent that if he permitted his slave for one day, he becomes permanently authorized until he re-interdicts him, because relinquishments are not time-bound. Then permission is established by explicit statement as well as by implication, as when he sees his slave buying and selling and remains silent, he becomes a ma'dhun according to us, contrary to Imam Zufar and al-Shafi'i. There is no difference whether he sells property owned by the master or by a stranger, with permission or without permission, a valid sale or an invalid one, because everyone who sees him considers him authorized in trade and contracts with him, then if he were not authorized, he would suffer loss. And if the master were not pleased with him, he would stop him to prevent harm from them. Commentary on 'therefore, he does not revert...': This refers back to what was said previously: 'and the slave after that acts for himself by his competency.' That is, after permission, since the slave acts with his competency, whatever liability befalls him does not revert to the master, meaning the master is not guarantor. And for this reason, because permission according to us is relinquishment of right, permission is not time-bound. To the extent that if he permits his slave for one day of trade, he becomes permanently permitted until the master re-interdicts him. The reason is that relinquishments are not time-bound. Question: If the mentioned permission is a relinquishment, then after relinquishment the master should not have the authority of interdiction, because he has dropped his right, and what is dropped does not return. Yet the master can still interdict after that. Answer: The authority of interdiction is due to the persistence of slavery. So after permission, the re-interdiction is a restraint on the right that he has with respect to the future, not that the dropped right returns. Question: The definition of permission is mentioned as: 'In the Shari'ah, it is the removal of interdiction and relinquishment of right.' Then how is inference from this valid? Answer: The mentioned inference is not on the definition itself, such that this objection arises that the definition does not accept inference, because definitions are of the genus of conceptions, and conception is not acquired by affirmation. Rather, the inference is on a subsidiary ruling: 'It was said: This definition is correct, this definition conforms to our principles.' And it is evident that these are rulings of affirmations upon which inference can be made.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage from the Hidayah commentary discusses the legal status of a slave permitted to trade (ma'dhun fi al-tijarah). The author begins by noting the difference between the Hanafi school and others (Zufar, Shafi'i, Ahmad) regarding the nature of permission. According to them, permission means appointing the slave as an agent, so the master can restrict the slave to a specific time or type of trade. According to Hanafis, permission is not agency but relinquishment of the master's right to interdict. Since the slave never lost his inherent legal capacity (ahliyah) for transactions—he has speech and intellect—the only barrier was the master's right to his neck and earnings. When the master permits, he drops that right, and the slave's inherent capacity becomes fully operative. Consequently, the slave transacts for himself, not as an agent, and the master cannot restrict the permission because relinquishments (isqatat) are not time-bound. The master is not liable for debts incurred by the slave, as they attach to the slave's own dhimmah. Regarding the proof of permission, it can be explicit or implied. If the master sees his slave engaging in trade and remains silent, this implies permission in the Hanafi view (opposed by Zufar and Shafi'i), because silence in the face of a transaction that would harm others indicates consent. The passage also addresses potential objections: if permission is relinquishment of the right to interdict, how can the master later re-interdict? The answer: the master's right to interdict is continuous due to the persistence of slavery; each moment grants a new right, and by granting permission he only waives the right for that moment, so he may reassert it later by explicit interdiction. Finally, a subtle point about definitions: the definition of permission as 'removal of interdiction and relinquishment of right' is a conceptual definition, not a proposition—inference is drawn not from the definition itself but from the subsidiary ruling that the definition is correct according to our principles.

Key Terms
مأذون (ma'dhun): A slave permitted by his master to engage in trade; after permission, he transacts on his own behalf with his inherent legal capacity.
إذن (idhn): The master's permission allowing the slave to trade; in Hanafi fiqh, it is a relinquishment (isqat) of the master's right to interdict the slave's transactions.
حجر (hajr): Legal interdiction preventing the slave from transacting; imposed due to the master's right over the slave's neck and earnings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a master gives his slave permission to trade for one day only, what is the legal effect?
A) The slave is authorized only for that day.
B) The slave becomes permanently authorized until the master explicitly re-interdicts him.
C) The permission is void because it is time-bound.
D) The slave is authorized only if he trades with the master's explicit consent each time.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi view that permission is a relinquishment (isqat) rather than agency (wakalah) leads to three key rulings: no time limitation, no master liability, and implied permission via silence.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
beginner
6 min
Scope of General Authorization for Slave Trade
Defining the scope of general authorization to trade

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the scope of a general trade authorization (idhn 'amm) for a slave, identify the underlying linguistic principle (ism jins), and apply it to determine which commercial acts are permissible.

Core Idea
A general authorization covers all trade-related transactions because 'tijarah' is a generic noun (ism jins) that implies generality.

Understanding the scope of a general authorization is key to knowing what a slave (or any agent) may do under such a permission. This lesson unpacks the classical Hanafi ruling on idhn 'amm, focusing on the linguistic reasoning that makes the permission broad and inclusive. By working through the text of Al-Quduri and its commentary, you will learn to parse the legal conditions and identify which transactions fall within the authorization.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Determine the act being ruled upon: the master giving a general authorization (idhn 'amm) to his slave. State the ruling: the slave's disposition in all trades becomes permissible (ja'iz).
The ruling is a permissibility (ibahah) of a wide range of actions, not a single act.
2
Parse the Condition
The authorization must be general and unrestricted. The master says, 'I have authorized you for trade' without specifying a particular type of trade or item. If restricted, the slave's authority is limited.
The condition is the absence of restriction.
3
Examine the Linguistic Reasoning (Ta'lil)
Identify the reason (ta'lil) given: the word 'tijarah' is an ism jins (generic noun) made definite by 'al-', which indicates generality (umum). In Hanafi usul, al- on a generic noun makes it 'amm, covering all instances of that genus.
This is a distinctive Hanafi linguistic principle; other schools may interpret al- differently.
4
List the Included Transactions
Based on the generality, the slave may engage in any customary commercial transaction: buying, selling, appointing agents, taking pledges, hiring, mudarabah, and even admitting debts or deposits, as all are considered part of trade (tijarah).
The Urdu commentary enumerates these examples explicitly.
5
Note Exclusions and Edge Cases
General authorization does not include acts that contradict the purpose of trade, such as the slave selling himself into slavery (self-sale), as that would nullify the authorization.
The common misunderstanding is that everything is allowed, but self-sale is explicitly excluded.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال. واذا اذن المولى لعبده في التجارة اذنا عاما جاز تصرفه في سائر التجارات ومعنى هذه المسألة ان يقول له اذنت لك فى التجارة ولا يقيده ووجهه ان التجارة اسم عام يتناول الجنس فيبيع ويشترى ما بدا له من انواع الاعيان لانه اصل التجارة
ترجمہ جب اجازت دے دی آقا نے اپنے غلام کو تجارت کی عام اجازت تو جائز ہوگا اس کا تصرف جملہ تجارات میں اور اس مسئلہ کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ آقا غلام سے یہ کہے کہ میں نے تجھے تجارت کی اجازت دے دی اور اس کو مقید نہ کرے اور وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ تجارت اسم
عام ہے جو جنس تجارت کو شامل ہے۔ پس غلام بیچے اور خرید لے جو اس کا جی چاہے انواع اشیاء میں سے کیونکہ یہی اصل تجارت ہے۔ تشریح قوله واذا اذن .. الخ اگر آقا نے اپنے غلام کو عام اجازت دی کسی معین چیز یا خاص قسم کی تجارت کے ساتھ مقید نہیں کیا۔ مثلاً یوں کہا کہ میں نے تجھے تجارت کی اجازت دے دی۔ تو غلام ہر قسم کی تجارت کا مجاز ہوگا یعنی اس کے لئے خرید نا ، فروخت کرنا ، وکیل بنانا، رہن لینا، اجرت پر لینا ، مضاربت کرنا ، دین یا ودیعت یا غصب کا اقرار کرنا ۔ غرض تمام تصرفات جائز ہیں ۔ کیونکہ آقا کے قول ۔ اذنت لک فی التجارة " میں لفظ تجارت اسم جنس محلی بالسلام ہے تو یہ عام ہوئی ۔ لہذ اجملہ انواع تجارت ولوازم تجارت کو شامل ہوگی۔
He (al-Quduri) said: When the master authorizes his slave for trade with a general authorization, his disposition in all trades is permissible. The meaning of this issue is that he says to him, 'I have authorized you for trade,' and does not restrict it. The reason is that 'trade' is a general term encompassing the genus. So he sells and buys whatever types of goods he wishes because that is the essence of trade.
Translation: When the master gives his slave a general authorization for trade, then his disposal in all trades is valid. The meaning of this issue is that the master says to the slave: 'I have authorized you for trade' and does not restrict him. The reason is that the word 'trade' is a common noun (ism jins) that includes all types of trade. So the slave sells and buys whatever he wishes from various kinds of items, because that is the essence of trade.
Explanation: If the master gives his slave a general authorization, not restricted to a specific item or particular type of trade – for example, he says, 'I have authorized you for trade' – then the slave is authorized for all types of trade. That is, for him, buying, selling, appointing an agent, taking a pledge (rahn), hiring, engaging in mudarabah, admitting a debt, deposit, or usurpation – in short, all dispositions are permissible. Because the master's statement 'I authorized you for trade' contains the word 'tijarah' which is a common noun definite by the definite article, so it is general. Hence it includes all types of trade and their necessary concomitants.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage explains the effect of a general authorization (idhn 'amm) given by a master to his slave. When the master says, 'I have authorized you for trade' without any restriction, the slave is permitted to engage in any type of trade and all customary transactions related to trade. The key linguistic point: the word 'tijarah' (trade) is an ism jins (generic noun) made definite by the definite article 'al-', which gives it generality (umum). This means the slave can buy, sell, appoint agents, take pledges, hire, enter into mudarabah, even admit debts or deposits – essentially all commercial dispositions that aim at profit. The text from Al-Hidayah (via the Urdu commentary) enumerates these examples. The underlying logic is that the essence of trade encompasses all these activities. This ruling is part of the Hanafi law of ma'dhun.

Key Terms
اذن عام (idhn 'amm): Unrestricted permission from the master to the slave for trade, covering all types of commercial activities.
اسم جنس (ism jins): A generic noun that by being definite (with 'al-') indicates generality (umum) covering all instances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master says to his slave 'I have authorized you for trade' without any restriction, which of the following is NOT permissible according to the Hanafi school?
A) Selling goods.
B) Appointing an agent to sell.
C) Taking a loan on credit.
D) Selling himself into slavery.

Key Takeaway
A general trade authorization (idhn 'amm) permits all commercial transactions because the word 'tijarah' is a generic noun (ism jins) indicating generality, except acts that contradict the purpose of trade such as self-sale.
